<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1079920637302292531 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1079920637302292531><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/105378403699408896/6ad9a21f4adaeee654f83a08a1327a68.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author style=color:rgb(231,76,60) title=emikachi>emily</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1079857001787564172')"> on the topic of dbt - can anyone advise on techniques to conform data to a unified base model in a multitenant situation?

for example, client A and client B provide similar information but with subtle (or indeed major) differences between how it is represented, so it makes sense to have a bespoke stage to transform their data to a standard <em>interface</em>, which then has a universal dbt model attached to it to build out interesting things.

does it make sense to think of this in terms of separate models? how could the nuts and bolts of realising this work? git submodules? </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=armslegshandsfeet data-user-id=466248882335252500>armslegshandsfeet</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, February 27, 2023 9:19 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1079920637302292531>2/27/2023 9:19 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Is the issue that the schema differ between clients, or the semantics differ within identical schema?</span></div></div></div></div></div>

We can do some unit testing and integration testing- but all those get us is that the data pipelines succeed or not.  While a successful data pipeline execution is great, I don&#39;t think we&#39;re done testing.

Specifically, we need to make sure the output data is &quot;as expected&quot;. Stuff like:
<ul><li>All user_ids are unique.</li></ul><ul><li>A field is not more than 50% null.</li></ul><ul><li>The API response codes don&#39;t contain a critical amount of 400s</li></ul><ul><li>Etc...</li></ul>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1080843243073310800 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1080843243073310800><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/697172923739406527/4bdca7d6972dd13eabe9339211d024de.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/0.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=minhdao97>minh_dao</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1080789091249033257')"> Hi everyone. I&#39;m having a question about snowflake schema for data warehouse.

I&#39;ve been working as data engineer for a year. I usually define dimension and fact tables based on our data and business requirements. After that, I have to build ETL/ELT, clean raw data, transform data to corresponding dimension and fact. And then, join many dimension tables to 1 fact table to build only 1 chart, which results in nearly the same data after cleaned.

I&#39;m wondering if I really need this snowflake schema, rather than just storing all the cleaned and flattened data. Although dimension tables come with useful features, for e.g: date time and location dimensions, version history, etc; other dimension tables seem redundant.

So, what should I do in this situation? What is the best practice in designing data warehouse nowadays?

Thank you very much! </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=sam_extra_1 data-user-id=697172923739406527>Sam</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, March 2, 2023 10:25 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1080843243073310800>3/2/2023 10:25 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Data warehousing(Dimensional modeling) involves storing massive amounts of data alongside fast retrieval. Beside this,
Data warehousing also provides an understandable table structure for business users e.g. DIM_DATE, DIM_USER, etc.

The main purpose of data warehouse design is to optimize the analytics query workload having millions of rows.
Traditional warehouses hadn&#39;t had the power they have now. Since the traditional warehouse is not capable of this much processing
on flattened data, that&#39;s why the data warehousing approach comes into the picture.

Now, the question is, current data warehouses are capable of processing billions of unstructured rows, so why do we still need this design?
The answer to me is, data warehouse design provides the table structure that suits the creation of optimized analytics query, and it&#39;s easy to understand by other data analytics and business intelligence user.
Also, there are other benefits of data warehousing which I have not mentioned,  this answer is more regarding your question.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1080846201257197619 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1080846201257197619><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=armslegshandsfeet data-user-id=466248882335252500>armslegshandsfeet</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, March 2, 2023 10:36 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1080846201257197619>3/2/2023 10:36 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Well said. If your data doesn&#39;t change at all, there&#39;s no real reason you wouldn&#39;t just use OBT most of the time. There&#39;s no incentive to put in the modeling work. But if you allow attributes to evolve over time, splitting off dimensions makes that work so much easier.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1080846808529506335 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1080846808529506335><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, March 2, 2023 10:39 AM">10:39 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>It&#39;s much easier to join to a dimensional identifier and a date (or date range) to a dimension than having to do a self-join on an entire denormalized table, both in terms of compute and in terms of query complexity.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1080853017550651392 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1080853017550651392><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/697172923739406527/4bdca7d6972dd13eabe9339211d024de.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=armslegshandsfeet>armslegshandsfeet</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1080846201257197619')"> Well said. If your data doesn&#39;t change at all, there&#39;s no real reason you wouldn&#39;t just use OBT most of the time. There&#39;s no incentive to put in the modeling work. But if you allow attributes to evolve over time, splitting off dimensions makes that work so much easier. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(52,152,219) title=notobiedog data-user-id=267610179862921216>electrified-ash-storm</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, March 2, 2023 1:40 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1080892395182370877>3/2/2023 1:40 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>OBT?</span></div></div></div></div></div>

I&#39;ve tried using coalesce(10), but it takes so long that it&#39;s unmanageable. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=philliphenry data-user-id=462278067474137088>PhillHenry</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, March 4, 2023 8:45 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1081542955854204958>3/4/2023 8:45 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>The <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">partitionBy</code> is partially undoing the <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">repartition</code>. 
The <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">repartition(10)</code> splits the <em>data frame</em> into 10 partitions.
The <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">partitionBy</code> will split the data <em>when written to disk</em> into folders based on the <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">Year</code> and <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">Month</code> values it contains.
Within those folders, the number of files will be a function of the number of executor threads that are operating on data that falls into that folder. Each executor thread will be writing to its own file(s).</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1082236666661568552 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1082236666661568552><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/527614767674687488/2c224d7c6b2f8913990bcb0f6caee8ec.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/331102813713203201/d7b2650199ce22862650cf8ca5d28495.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=gratisimo>monert151</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1082212546133622784')"> Whats the difference between failover database vs read database? </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=hadouken_1 data-user-id=527614767674687488>Hadouken!</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, March 6, 2023 6:42 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1082236666661568552>3/6/2023 6:42 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>ChatGPT to the rescue:
<div class="chatlog__markdown-quote"><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-border"></div><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-content">A failover database is a backup database that can be activated in case of a primary database failure or disaster&#185;. A read database is a secondary database that can be used for read-only queries while the primary database handles write operations&#178;.
</div></div>
I&#39;ll just add that typically you can&#39;t do both with one instance. The failover is typically inaccessible, and the read replica typically can&#39;t be switched to read/write.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Monday, March 6, 2023 11:15 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1084045876298780755 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1084045876298780755><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/232126709384740865/034a7453db466bf6cc13b91f1a901796.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=thedro54 data-user-id=232126709384740865>theDro</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, March 11, 2023 6:31 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1084045876298780755>3/11/2023 6:31 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>General question here. I&#39;m always on the lookout for ways to improve my code, and I know the &quot;single responsibility principal&quot; is important when thinking about trying to write things functionally, but at what point can I stop trying to break my functions down?

One of the things people say is &quot;succinctly define your function, if it has the word &quot;and&quot; in, then it should be broken down&quot;)

Example: I have a function <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">get_all_endpoint_data</code> which handles the looping of an API endpoint (by the definition above, it doesn&#39;t have AND in and therefore it has a single responsibility). The function itself 1) makes an initial call to the endpoint, if there is no pagination, it returns the results 2) if there is pagination, runs a  <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">while</code> loop, updating the results each time and finally returning them.

In this example, does it make sense that this is a single function?</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1084047589260935169 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1084047589260935169><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/161154369763409921/d760257b5ffd16af7a8fa7056574cc51.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(46,204,113) title=kahnwong data-user-id=161154369763409921>kahnwong</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, March 11, 2023 6:38 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1084047589260935169>3/11/2023 6:38 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Another rule of thumb is, a function should do only one thing</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1084047667702804530 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1084047667702804530><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, March 11, 2023 6:38 AM">6:38 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>So in this case your function looks good</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>3</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

<code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--multiline language-py">def process_chunk(chunk: list[dict]) -&gt; list[dict]:
  ...

data: Generator[list[dict]] = (batch.to_pylist() for batch in ds.dataset().to_batches())
for chunk in data:
  new_chunk = process_chunk(chunk)
  ds.dataset().write(pyarrow.batch.from_pylist(new_chunk)</code>
(the writing is more eficcient than shown in this pseudo code, but the point is that it needs to create a C array/batch from a list of python objects)
 so for each chunk it does: <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">C-array -&gt; python-list -&gt; C-array</code></span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Sunday, March 26, 2023 9:29 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1089525224480977016 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1089525224480977016><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Sunday, March 26, 2023 9:24 AM">9:24 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>makes sense?</span></div></div></div></div></div>

def greater_than_one(data: DataFrame) -&gt; DataFrame:

  return data

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1090662354443833365 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1090662354443833365><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/698372956618883112/5d3817ac6297dda6763f5bc3e7e0db30.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=liquidityblocks data-user-id=698372956618883112>numberstonarratives</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, March 29, 2023 12:42 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1090662354443833365>3/29/2023 12:42 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>When naming a datetime column, is there a good rule on using &quot;created_on&quot; vs &quot;start_date&quot;?</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1090666851958280282 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1090666851958280282><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/795717019529510954/d7ac807c84cc351cc2575c7aeba685a1.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rue.de.chateau data-user-id=795717019529510954>rue.de.chateau</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, March 29, 2023 1:00 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1090666851958280282>3/29/2023 1:00 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I don&#39;t see those columns as synonymous. For example, we have a <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">contract</code> table at work, and each row has a <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_on</code> column indicating when the contract was created/signed, which is usually very different from when the contract actually starts. So we have both <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_on_date</code> and <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">start_date</code> in the same table indicating different things. In short, I see <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_on</code> more like a metadata column to facilitate ETLs downstream whereas <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">start_date</code> is truly a dimension for whatever you&#39;re describing.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1090669047252779119 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1090669047252779119><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/376219375994273795/a_3b3f21e57e3942035291491a347fea55.gif?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/795717019529510954/d7ac807c84cc351cc2575c7aeba685a1.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=rue.de.chateau>rue.de.chateau</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1090666851958280282')"> I don&#39;t see those columns as synonymous. For example, we have a <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">contract</code> table at work, and each row has a <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_on</code> column indicating when the contract was created/signed, which is usually very different from when the contract actually starts. So we have both <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_on_date</code> and <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">start_date</code> in the same table indicating different things. In short, I see <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_on</code> more like a metadata column to facilitate ETLs downstream whereas <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">start_date</code> is truly a dimension for whatever you&#39;re describing. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=sud0x90 data-user-id=376219375994273795>ZeroOneFive</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, March 29, 2023 1:09 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1090669047252779119>3/29/2023 1:09 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>This. Totally this. In our architecture, I made it a hard rule to always reserve <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_at</code> and <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">updated_at</code> for datetime columns in UTC for the timestamps related to the record, <em>not</em> to whatever the record contains.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1090669221677125632 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1090669221677125632><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Wednesday, March 29, 2023 1:10 PM">1:10 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>There&#39;s a plethora of words that can be used for all the other events in a record. Similar to our sales schema, contracts have <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">signed_at</code>, <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">amended_at</code>, etc.</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup_tone4><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍🏾 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d-1f3fe.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1090672171468210216 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1090672171468210216><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/128715643204796416/439b7d8ce2e8e4e4f2e2dbf95df46ea7.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=compeanansi data-user-id=128715643204796416>CompeAnansi</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, March 29, 2023 1:21 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1090672171468210216>3/29/2023 1:21 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>we also use created_at instead of created_on, but im not sure it matters, so long as the chosen suffix is used consistently.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1090681415663894558 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1090681415663894558><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/609001022576132119/d078eb373aea7a8d6c37cf29a5cc5d1e.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=phobia42 data-user-id=609001022576132119>Phobia42</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, March 29, 2023 1:58 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1090681415663894558>3/29/2023 1:58 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>That&#39;s why I prefer &quot;created_date&quot; to remove all ambiguity.  Also always put it as the very last column of the table, so it feels more &quot;metadata&quot; than actual data</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1090681729347489822 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1090681729347489822><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Wednesday, March 29, 2023 1:59 PM">1:59 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Where things got really fun on a recent project is where we needed &quot;source_modify_date&quot;, &quot;load_modify_date&quot; and &quot;modify_date&quot; to track 3 different pieces of information.  But we stopped there so we didn&#39;t wind up with 13 metadata fields, lol</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1090684465673678969 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1090684465673678969><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/376219375994273795/a_3b3f21e57e3942035291491a347fea55.gif?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/609001022576132119/d078eb373aea7a8d6c37cf29a5cc5d1e.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=phobia42>Phobia42</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1090681415663894558')"> That&#39;s why I prefer &quot;created_date&quot; to remove all ambiguity.  Also always put it as the very last column of the table, so it feels more &quot;metadata&quot; than actual data </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=sud0x90 data-user-id=376219375994273795>ZeroOneFive</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, March 29, 2023 2:10 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1090684465673678969>3/29/2023 2:10 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>In my experience, <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_date</code> is slightly inferior to <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_at</code> because <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">at</code> denotes a time. So I can expect it to have a timestamp. <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">_date</code>, if the actual column has a timestamp, would be misleading. I would agree, however, that should you want an actual date column, <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">_date</code> should be used. But then at I&#39;ll do it like <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_at_date</code>. Where <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">_at</code> wins for me, personally, is when I localize the timestamp. So I can do something like <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_at</code> and <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_at_local</code>. And if you extend the practice further, they become <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_at_date</code> and <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_at_local_date</code>, which I believe are significantly unambiguous.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Wednesday, March 29, 2023 2:12 PM">(edited)</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1090703009245298828 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1090703009245298828><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/698372956618883112/5d3817ac6297dda6763f5bc3e7e0db30.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/795717019529510954/d7ac807c84cc351cc2575c7aeba685a1.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=rue.de.chateau>rue.de.chateau</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1090666851958280282')"> I don&#39;t see those columns as synonymous. For example, we have a <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">contract</code> table at work, and each row has a <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_on</code> column indicating when the contract was created/signed, which is usually very different from when the contract actually starts. So we have both <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_on_date</code> and <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">start_date</code> in the same table indicating different things. In short, I see <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_on</code> more like a metadata column to facilitate ETLs downstream whereas <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">start_date</code> is truly a dimension for whatever you&#39;re describing. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=liquidityblocks data-user-id=698372956618883112>numberstonarratives</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, March 29, 2023 3:24 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1090703009245298828>3/29/2023 3:24 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Very helpful example! Thank you for your perspective!</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Wednesday, March 29, 2023 3:24 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1090703573790240879 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1090703573790240879><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/698372956618883112/5d3817ac6297dda6763f5bc3e7e0db30.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/376219375994273795/a_3b3f21e57e3942035291491a347fea55.gif?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=sud0x90>ZeroOneFive</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1090669047252779119')"> This. Totally this. In our architecture, I made it a hard rule to always reserve <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">created_at</code> and <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">updated_at</code> for datetime columns in UTC for the timestamps related to the record, <em>not</em> to whatever the record contains. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=liquidityblocks data-user-id=698372956618883112>numberstonarratives</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, March 29, 2023 3:26 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1090703573790240879>3/29/2023 3:26 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>That&#39;s a nice distinction. Basically, use &quot;created_at&quot; to manage records in the table and &quot;start_date (time)&quot; to manage events or information depicted by the record</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1090704417973620747 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1090704417973620747><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Wednesday, March 29, 2023 3:29 PM">3:29 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Is there a good rule to choose singular vs plural table names? <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1092782504664117382 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1092782504664117382><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=armslegshandsfeet data-user-id=466248882335252500>armslegshandsfeet</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, April 4, 2023 9:07 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1092782504664117382>4/4/2023 9:07 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>So, another approach to the SCD paradigm was outlined by Maxime Beauchemin: <a href="https://maximebeauchemin.medium.com/functional-data-engineering-a-modern-paradigm-for-batch-data-processing-2327ec32c42a">https://maximebeauchemin.medium.com/functional-data-engineering-a-modern-paradigm-for-batch-data-processing-2327ec32c42a</a></span></div><div class=chatlog__embed><div class="chatlog__embed-color-pill chatlog__embed-color-pill--default"></div><div class=chatlog__embed-content-container><div class=chatlog__embed-content><div class=chatlog__embed-text><div class=chatlog__embed-title><a class=chatlog__embed-title-link href=https://maximebeauchemin.medium.com/functional-data-engineering-a-modern-paradigm-for-batch-data-processing-2327ec32c42a><div class="chatlog__markdown chatlog__markdown-preserve">Functional Data Engineering — a modern paradigm for batch data proc...</div></a></div><div class=chatlog__embed-description><div class="chatlog__markdown chatlog__markdown-preserve">Batch data processing — historically known as ETL — is extremely challenging. It’s time-consuming, brittle, and often unrewarding. Not only…</div></div></div><div class=chatlog__embed-thumbnail-container><a class=chatlog__embed-thumbnail-link href=https://images-ext-1.discordapp.net/external/QVQHCHOSG7nymlxV7KpL4ioisGIgTVsX1z1_7PIDibQ/https/miro.medium.com/v2/resize%3Afit%3A1200/1%2AwLRaUmtskDynbqGklT8Lkw.jpeg> <img class=chatlog__embed-thumbnail src=https://images-ext-1.discordapp.net/external/QVQHCHOSG7nymlxV7KpL4ioisGIgTVsX1z1_7PIDibQ/https/miro.medium.com/v2/resize%3Afit%3A1200/1%2AwLRaUmtskDynbqGklT8Lkw.jpeg alt=Thumbnail loading=lazy> </a></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1092782790258470942 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1092782790258470942><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Tuesday, April 4, 2023 9:08 AM">9:08 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>So your dimensions are snapshotted by date. <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1093644633751429141 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1093644633751429141><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/5.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=paxos7775 data-user-id=1038924343415148566>Paxos</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, April 6, 2023 6:13 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1093644633751429141>4/6/2023 6:13 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I was sort of being sarcastic; I don&#39;t think it&#39;s inherently bad, I&#39;m just not a fan personally.

I don&#39;t really appreciate the box dbt makes you operate in, and I think it tries too hard to be overly prescriptive. I think dbt would be perfect if you stripped out the &quot;model building&quot; aspects and kept everything else as a query dependency/lineage tool.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1093645299790123028 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1093645299790123028><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/113136451457146880/0275ef289c9e7b6338d7b72e8f4f2fca.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=i_._i data-user-id=113136451457146880>dean</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, April 6, 2023 6:15 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1093645299790123028>4/6/2023 6:15 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I think dbt is a fantastic tool for data modeling, a thing I don’t really like doing</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1093646014897999932 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1093646014897999932><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/5.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=paxos7775 data-user-id=1038924343415148566>Paxos</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, April 6, 2023 6:18 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1093646014897999932>4/6/2023 6:18 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Also there&#39;s a bunch of minor gripes I have that make using it feel like death by a thousand paper cuts:
<ul><li>Model runs hold super long transactions</li><li>You&#39;re limited to the model config options dbt prescribes to you depending on your DWH instead of abstracting operations</li><li>It encourages monolithic data models with spagettified dependencies</li><li>extending dbt with Jinja feels weird, but is encouraged</li></ul>
etc</span></div></div></div></div></div>

This becomes problematic when your entire data ecosystem is founded on such a house of cards.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1093648113249562644 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1093648113249562644><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, April 6, 2023 6:27 PM">6:27 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Not that you can&#39;t use Databricks using SWE/DE best practices, but most Databricks shops I&#39;ve seen do not.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
